Divine Transcendence
beginner
3 min
Multiple Valid Interpretations: Specifying or Delegating?
Sanusi presents the two madhhabs on multiple valid interpretations after ta'wil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two scholarly positions on handling multiple valid interpretations of a verse whose apparent meaning is impossible.

Core Idea
When multiple interpretations are valid, scholars differ: specify one to remove confusion or delegate to Allah.

This lesson addresses a subtle but important question: what if after turning away from an impossible literal meaning, a verse admits several equally valid interpretations? The passage presents two respected positions from Islamic scholarly tradition, each with its own rationale.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on multiple interpretations
Read the Arabic passage carefully. It presents a question: should we specify one interpretation or delegate the meaning?
Notice the contrasting words: 'yu'ayyan' vs 'yufawwad'.
2
Identify the two views
Identify the madhhab of Imam al-Haramayn and the madhhab of the early scholars. Note the reason given for each.
Imam al-Haramayn: to remove confusion. Early scholars: to avoid arbitrary judgment.
3
Compare the motivations
Think about why each position makes sense. What is the concern behind specifying? What is the concern behind delegating?
This is a classic difference in interpretive methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان ضوابط التأويل ، ومتى يُصار إليه ]
أما ما استحالَ ظاهرُهُ ؛ نحو : ﴿ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى ﴾ فإنَّا نصرفُهُ عن ظاهره اتفاقاً ، ثم إنْ كانَ له تأويل واحد تعيَّنَ الحمل عليهِ ، وإلا وجبَ التفويضُ معَ التنزيهِ ، وهو مذهب الأقدمينَ ، خلافاً لإمام الحرمين .
لمَّا ذكرَ أنَّ ما يُجوِّزُهُ العقل إذا أخبر الشرعُ بوقوعِهِ يجبُ أنْ يُؤْمَنَ بهِ على ظاهره ، ولا يجوز تأويلُه ؛ والتعرُّضُ لتأويله بدعة . . ذكرَ أَنَّ
عن
ما أخبر الشرعُ بهِ ، وكانَ ظاهرُهُ مستحيلاً عندَ العقل فإنَّا نصرفُهُ ظاهره المستحيل ؛ لأنَّا نعلم قطعاً أنَّ الشرع لا يخبر بوقوع ما لا يمكنُ وقوعه ، ولو كذبنا العقل في هذا ، وعملنا بظاهرِ النقل المستحيل . . لأدَّى ذلك إلى انهدام النقلِ أيضاً ؛ لأنَّ العقل أصل لثبوتِ النبوَّاتِ التي يتفرّعُ عنها صحة النقل ، فيلزم إذاً مِنْ تكذيب العقل تكذيب النقل .
ثم بعد صرْفِ اللفظ عن ظاهره المستحيل :
إنْ لم يكن له بعد ذلكَ إلا تأويل واحد صحيح .. تعيَّنَ الحمل عليه ؛ لعدم وجودِ غيره ؛ وذلكَ مثل قوله : ( وَهُوَ مَعَكُمْ أَيْنَ مَا كُنتُمْ ) [الحديد : ٤] فَإِنَّهُ يستحيلُ حملُهُ على ظاهرِهِ مِنَ المصاحبة بالذاتِ ، ولم يبقَ بعد ذلك إلا حمله على المعيَّة بالعلم والرعاية ونظيره :
إِلَّا هُوَ رَابِعُهُمْ ... [المجادلة : ٧] الآيةَ ، ونحو ذلك مما هو كثير
وإِنْ كانَ لهُ بعد ذلك تأويلات ، كلُّ واحدٍ منها مستقيم ؛ فهل يُعيَّنُ واحدٌ منها ليندفعَ اللَّبْسُ عن العوام ، وهو مذهب إمام الحرمين عنِ التعيين ويُفوَّضُ الأمرُ فيهِ إلى اللهِ تعالى دفعاً للتحكُّم ، وهو مذهب الأقدمينَ ؟
Statement of the rules of ta'wil (interpretation), and when it should be applied. As for that whose apparent meaning is impossible, like {He established Himself upon the Throne} (20:5), we turn it away from its apparent meaning by consensus. Then if it has one valid interpretation, it must be taken upon that; otherwise, tafwid (delegation) together with tanzih (transcendence) is obligatory, and that is the madhhab of the early scholars, contrary to Imam al-Haramayn. When he mentioned that what reason deems possible, if revelation informs of its occurrence, must be believed in its apparent meaning, and its ta'wil is not permissible, and attempting its ta'wil is an innovation... he mentioned that what revelation informs of, and its apparent meaning is impossible according to reason, then we turn it away from its impossible apparent meaning, because we know with certainty that revelation does not inform of the occurrence of what cannot occur. If we were to deny reason in this, and act upon the apparent meaning of the impossible transmitted text, that would lead to the demolition of the transmitted text as well, because reason is the basis for establishing prophethood from which the soundness of transmission derives; so from discrediting reason necessarily follows discrediting transmission. Then after turning the word away from its impossible apparent meaning: if it has no valid interpretation other than one, then it must be taken upon that, because there is no other; and that is like His saying: {And He is with you wherever you are} (57:4) — it is impossible to take it upon its apparent meaning of essential companionship, and there remains after that only taking it upon companionship by knowledge and care, and its like: {Except He is the fourth of them} (58:7), and similar things that are many. And if after that it has interpretations, each of which is valid, then is one specified to remove confusion from the common people – which is the madhhab of Imam al-Haramayn – or is the matter delegated to Allah Almighty to avoid arbitrary judgment – which is the madhhab of the early scholars?
Source pages p. 625

Commentary
This passage explains the rules of ta'wil (interpretation) when the apparent meaning of a revealed text is impossible according to reason. The author begins by stating that when the apparent meaning is impossible (like 'establishing Himself on the Throne' which suggests physical location), all scholars agree that we must turn away from that apparent meaning. Then, after turning away, if there is only one valid interpretation, it must be adopted; otherwise, tafwid (delegating the meaning to Allah) along with tanzih (affirming transcendence) is obligatory. This is the position of the early scholars, contrary to Imam al-Haramayn. The author then provides the logical reason for this: we know with certainty that revelation cannot report something impossible, and if we were to reject reason in this, we would also destroy transmission because reason is the foundation for confirming prophethood. After giving the general principle, he gives examples: verses about God's 'withness' (ma'iyya) cannot mean literal spatial companionship, so they must be interpreted as knowledge and care. Then he raises the case of multiple valid interpretations: should one be specified to remove confusion (Imam al-Haramayn's view) or should the matter be delegated to Allah (the early scholars' view)? The passage ends with this question, leaving the two positions presented.

Key Terms
التأويل (ta'wil)
التفويض (tafwid)
التنزيه (tanzih)
التعيين (specifying)
العوام (common people)
التحكم (arbitrary judgment)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think there is only one valid interpretation for every verse.
Correction: The passage shows that scholars acknowledged the possibility of multiple valid interpretations and differed on how to handle them.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason given for the early scholars' position of delegating the meaning to Allah?
A) To remove confusion from the common people.
B) To avoid arbitrary judgment.
C) Because there is no valid interpretation.
D) Because Imam al-Haramayn opposed it.

Key Takeaway
When multiple valid interpretations exist, scholars disagree on whether to specify one or delegate the meaning to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a difficult verse in the Quran, do you rush to find a single meaning to settle your heart, or are you comfortable trusting that Allah knows best even when you cannot decide? Which approach reflects greater humility, and why does your instinct lean one way?
?
The early scholars chose to avoid arbitrary judgment (tahakkum) by delegating meaning to Allah. Where in your own life do you force certainty or closure when God has left room for mystery? How might that be a subtle form of tahakkum?
?
If you were to teach this passage to someone confused about a verse, would you specify an interpretation to give them peace, or would you leave it open and teach them to trust Allah's knowledge? Which choice shows more love for that person's faith?
